2.1.3 Other environmental and socially important impacts 
From a LCA perspective, the project concept provides a very promising way to reduce the emissions of greenhouse gases (CO2) 
in terms of kg CO2 abated per kg of OFMSW treated to Bioethanol, Ethylene, biopolymers and additives, compared to other fossil-
fuel-based alternatives. The exact amount of th e reduction of the overall GWP will be calculated as part of the LCA that will be 
carried out based on the results provided by the project, but there are several items indicating a positive balance in terms of kg 
CO2 abated per kg of OFMSW treated: 
1. The project entails the production of new biobased products from OFMSW which can be considered alternative to similar fossil-
fuels-based products. For example, the project proposes the production of high value microalgae amino acids on the base of N 
and CO2 directly recovered from OFMSW, which is an alternative to the high carbon foot print protein crops using of synthesis 
fertilizers, 
2. The CO2 generated during the biopolymers degradation is carbon neutral in contrast to equivalent fossil-fuel-based polymers, 
3. The exhausted CO2 from biofuel combustion is carbon neutral,  
4. The system entails the production of renewable power sources such as the biogas, 
5. The low energy intensity of this type of process compared to conventional management systems based on AD, composting 
and incineration technologies. Mixed culture PHA from industrial waste water has been shown to have a lower GWP than HDPE, 
assuming a high concentration or COD 54. The results from Kendall 55 (for PHA from waste) show a lower non-renewable energy 
use than petrochemical plastics. 
6. Finally, as the extraction of PHA will be carried out using non -toxic dissolvent (alkaline-acid solutions, green dissolvent), the 
conventional recovery operation (normally based on thermal distillation techniques) is not required.  
In addition to environmental importance, it is necessary consider social importance of the project. European waste management 
sector currently employs around 1 million people (source PSIRU) and the anaerobic digestion sector employs over 70,000 people 
according to EBA (European Biogas Association) but there is still a wide potential for a lot more employment growth through 
adequate treatment of organic fraction of MSW in order to obtain chemical building blocks, b iopolymers and additives by 
implementing the proposed new bio-based value chains.  
Regarding direct job creation, highly qualified staff specialized in obtaining the new products will be necessary to carried out the 
proposed activities. Moreover, the URBIOFIN demonstration activities are expected to create 18 highly qualified direct jobs among 
the project partners during the project. After that, the future development of the project concept will allow transforming millions of 
tonnes of organic municipal waste into valuable products. Different companies from several countries will be necessary to carry 
out the transformation from the obtained chemical building blocks or polymers to new bio -based products. As a result, not only 
operators or process biological experts but also sales personal will be required to manage the output of the mentioned building 
blocks and raw materials in an international market. After the project, the new bio -based value chains and business will 
require the recruitment of 15 -20 new te chnicians in the involved companies to manage the production of the bio -based 
products and their future commercialization.

There is also a huge potential to create new indirect jobs related to the growth of new markets for these new biobased products, 
their future commercialization and product distribution within the involved bio-based economy clusters and final user industries of 
the European circular economy. 
Moreover, the project will contribute to the adoption of new models for OFMSW management since it  provides a competitive 
conversion of mentioned wastes to bioproducts. Therefore, it is aligned with the EU Bioeconomy Strategy which addresses the 
production of renewable biological resources and their conversion into vital products and bio-energy. It will contribute not only in 
scaling up of new technologies and processes for the bioeconomy but also in developing markets and competitiveness in 
bioeconomy sectors.  
The processes involved in the project will be interconnected so that a versatile and efficient biorefinery for OFMSW will be 
demonstrated. Bio-based industries involving research and innovation focused on the sustainable use of organic waste 
for the produc tion of bio -based products would be boosted thanks to the development of the proposed concept and 
thus making possible an improvement of the competitiveness in European Bioeconomy sector as well as to diversify in 
current models of biorefineries in EU Member states. 
By using the biorefinery concept applied to OFMSW (urban biorefinery), organic waste will be further exploited as feedstock which 
currently is not wide and properly valorised along EU. The development of biotechnological processes included in th e project 
such us anaerobic digestion or bioethanol fermentation, among others, are a vital part of the European bio-economy tapping into 
organic municipal solid waste to produce high value added products. In particular, it will be taken into account its h eterogeneity 
and variable composition, to produce different valuable marketable products. Then, required logistics and supply chain for a 
cascading-in-value/-in-time56 use of the waste streams would be developed along the project and it will contribute to the shift 
towards a resource -efficient, low-carbon economy to achieve sustainable growth (resource -efficient Europe flagship initiative, 
Europe Strategy 2020).   
Municipalities and companies dealing with organic waste management, in addition to their fees for treating this material, can 
increase their revenue by producing chemical building blocks, biopolymers, additives and/or fertilisers. Helping at the same time 
to fulfil the requirements of Waste Framework Directive which urges to member states by 2020 to take the necessary measures 
to achieve the targets of re-use and recycling of domestic waste and move towards a European recycling society with a high level 
of resource efficiency. Thus, reducing the organic materials that currently are sent to landfills  and, consequently, not converted 
into valuable products.  
Additionally as it is stated by European Biogas Association, anaerobic digestion is an important pillar of the European circu lar 
economy: it mitigates GHG emissions, recycles nutrients in the form of organic fertilisers, prevents nitrogen leakage into 
groundwater and avoids the spread of harmful diseases through landfilling.

3. Implementation
3.1 Work plan  
3.1.1 Overall structure of the work plan 
The project is composed by 8 work packages; each one follows a logical phase of the project. There is one work package (WP1) 
which addresses all preliminary actions for the urban biorefinery design. Four mainly technical, demonstration and validation work 
packages (WP2-WP5) and three work packages which support project activities as integration of results, LCA, LCC regulatory 
assessments (WP6); communication, dissemination and exploitation activities (WP7) and project management (WP8). The inter-
relation between the different work packages and Gantt chart are below.

3.1.2 Business plan 
The URBIONFIN business model has a whole value chain approach which integrates the business ambitions of the participant 
company partners including technology providers but also the bio-based products end users. 
Using CANVAS methodology the business plan proposed is detailed in further pages: 
Value proposition. Despite the improvements in sorting and recycling, a large fraction of Municipal Solid Waste (MSW) is still 
landfilled (31%) or incinerated (26%) across Europe. This practice is posing environmental concerns, as well as wasting potentially 
useful resources contained in MSW. Commission adopted in December 2015 an ambitious new Circular Economy Package. The 
revised legislative proposal on waste sets clear targets for reduction of waste and establishes an ambitious and credible lon g-
term path for waste management and recycling. To ensure effective implementation, the waste reduction targets in the new 
proposal are accompanied by concrete measures to address obstacles on the ground and the different situations across Member 
States. Key elements of the revised waste proposal include: 
✓ A common EU target for recycling 65% of municipal waste by 2030; 
✓ A binding landfill target to reduce landfill to maximum of 10% of municipal waste by 2030; 
✓ A ban on landfilling of separately collected waste; 
✓ Promotion of economic instruments to discourage landfilling; 
✓ Concrete measures to promote re-use and stimulate industrial symbiosis –turning one industry's by-product 
into another industry's raw material; 
✓ Economic incentives for producers to put greener products on the market and support recovery and recycling 
schemes (e.g. for packaging, batteries, electric and electronic equipment, vehicles). 
Differentiating and enlarging the biomass feedstock portfolio are key objectives of the bio -based industries in Europe. The 
abundance of sugars and other potentially interesting organic matter are identifying MSW as an alternative source of feedstock 
for the bioeconomy.  Exploiting MSW, one of many residual streams in today’s economic activities, as a biomass feedsto ck 
source, contributes to these goals. At the same time, utilizing MSW as a feedstock source for biorefineries helps realising the EU 
circular economy through industrial symbiosis, i.e. collaboration between producers to use each other’s by -products. The low 
economical value of state of the art recycled products from OFMSW like compost or biogas is limiting the sustainable 
implementation of separate sourcing systems since increasing citizen environmental (waste) taxes is then need to tackle important 
logistic costs. New biobased products can help to improve waste treatment environmental and socio-economical sustainability.   
What does URBIOFIN offer?. URBIOFIN project offers a feasible integrated biorefinery technological solution that converts 
OFMSW into valuable bioproducts. This new Biorefinery concept is composed by several integrated process technology units. 
The different interconnected modules that define URBIOFIN bio refinery are showed in previous Figure 1.3a. The biorefinery 
process units are adaptable to treat different MSW compositions, obtaining several marketable bioproducts as outputs. 
 
Table 3.1a Targeted biobased products to be obtained at demo scale during URBIOFIN project

Medium and long chain fatty acids (MCFA/LCFA) Chemical platform for mcl-PHA production

Advantages. URBIOFIN proposes an economical and technical feasible technology for the conversion of OFMSW by:  
✓ New bioBased products portfolio, as well as t echnology aligned with sustainability and waste EU -policies that 
minimizes the anthropogenic impact to the environment, contributes to the European sustainable bioeconomy and 
adds value in reducing European oil dependence, improving the innovation competitiveness of involved industries. 
✓ Economical feasibility . More positive than the competing technologies (composting, incineration and 
biomethanisation). No need to raise citizen´s environmental taxes or at less extent. The business analysis show a 
                                                                             BBI 2016-D6                                                
745785 URBIOFIN - Part B - 38 
 
 
rentability of the URBIOFIN model, current waste treatment technologies are profitable only with the application of 
the rate of waste treatment57. 
✓ Tailor made . M odular design projects for each client, covering the geographical, compositional and seasonal 
variability of OMSW.  Versatile. The different units comprising the b iorefinery can be adapted to current MSW 
treatment plants. 
✓ Proven pre-industrial processes. The technical experience with the different demonstration processes units after 
URBIOFIN project realisation will prove a stable and competitive biorefinery process at semi-industrial scale, ready 
for scaling up to industrial level.  
✓ The different units composing the biorefinery will be adapted for dif ferent market bioproducts demand and 
replicability of the biorefinery model worldwide. 
Market. URBIOFIN market has been analysed from two different points of view: 
- MSW Treatment market for the Biorefinery technology (input of the biorefinery) 
- Bioproducts market (output of the biorefinery). The analysis of bioproducts obtained in URBIOFIN biorefinery was 
analysed in the corresponding bioproducts business cases (annexed). 
According to EUROSTAT official statistics, EU -27 countries generated 239 million tones of Municipal Solid Waste in 2014 . 
Treatment strategies are identified based on reported amounts of municipal waste l andfilled (27 .6%), incinerated (26 .8%), 
recycled (27.6%), composted (15.9%) and other (2.1%). “Composting” is defined in this statistic report as a biological process 
that submits biodegradable waste to anaerobic or aerobic decomposition  and that results in a product used on land or for the 
production of growing media or substrates. In 2014, 38 million tones of OFMSW were converted into compost or biogas, 24 
millions more than in 1995. A continuous growth is shown over the last 10 years . In that year, average production was 475 
kg per capita (16% to compost and biogas) , ranging from 759 kg per capita in Denmark to 272 kg per capita in Poland and 
Romania. The variations reflect differences in consumption patterns and economic wealth, but also depend on how municipal 
waste is collected and managed. Globally municipal solid waste (MSW) generation is approximately 1.3 billion tonnes per year 
and this amount is expected to increase to 2.2 billion tonnes by 2025 58. MSW management in European countries has evolved 
over the last two decades from a focus on disposal methods to a greater focus on prevention, recycling and valorisation. Moving 
municipal waste management up the 'waste hierarchy' (i.e. waste prevention, preparing for reuse, recycling, recovery and 
disposal) is a key way of extracting more value from resources while reducing the pressures on the environment and creating 
jobs. The global market for bioproducts is expected to grow to $700.7 billion by 2018, with a five-year compound annual growth 
rate (CAGR) of 5.5%.  The non-energetic market, the fastest growing segment overall, is moving at a tremendous 14.9% CAGR. 
The non-energetic bioproducts category, which includes chemicals and materials, is the largest and fastest moving segment in 
this market and is expected to reach $472.8 billion by 2018, up from $236.3 billion in 2013 59.  The market size and current sales 
of bioproducts derived from URBIOFIN biorefinery are described in table 3.1b and more details appear in Addendum 1.

tones of OFMSW can be enough to cover an area of 1 million people. As in January 2016, EU populations was about 510 million 
people, potential market for “existing plants” could be estimated up to 500 plants. Assuming a similar growth tendency of the last 
10 years (1995-2014), OFMSW bioconversion could rise from 16% up to 32% in the next 10 years (upto 2024) derived from the 
circular economy package, bio -economy, and other policies, the overall number of plants potentially adapted or created as a 
URBIOFIN biorefinery would be 1,000 plants (50% existing and 50% news).

Existing alternatives. Current treatments technologies for OFMSW have been used for several years and are widely implanted 
technologies such as biomethanisation, composting or incineration. These technol ogies are considered as substitutive 
competitors of URBIOFIN. On the other hand, there are new MSW treatment technologies that can convert OFMSW into biofuels 
(direct competitors) (Figure 3.1c). 
 
Figure 3.1c Competitors of URBIOFIN: treatment technologies for OFMSW 
Out of all the MSW generated in the EU in 2014 (239 million tons, which correspond to 475 kg per capita), 27% is landfilled, 27% 
is recycled, 26% is incinerated, and 15% is composted60. 
Regarding direct competitors, there are several technologies for the conversion of OFMSW into second generation bioethanol 
and bioproducts, which are all of them at demonstration scale. Some of these  processes have been developed by Bluefire, 
Coskata, New Planet Energy or Fulcrum61. In these projects not only OFMSW is used as feedstock, but also agroindustrial wastes. 
The substrate is firstly pre -treated by thermochemical processes in order to make the cellulosic component accessible to the 
cellulases for t he subsequent enzymatic saccharification step. Sugars -mainly glucose - are released after the enzymatic 
hydrolysis and are then fermented to produce bioethanol or other intermediates. URBIOFIN offers a more complete exploitation 
of OFMSW resources.  
Customer segments. The main customers are the  EU local authorities (municipalities), which are responsible of OFMSW 
management. Statistics of MSW waste in the EU are offered in terms of kg per habitant or country as well as applied treatment 
(incineration, landfilling, composting or other). Behind this data there are a large number of local authorities or municipalities that 
alone or creating consortiums of more than one municipalities are responsible of MSW waste treatment. But, in  practice, 
municipalities normally use owned public or private waste companies to run MSW treatment plants. Access to building or 
exploitation contracts is only possible through public tenders. There are two possible scenarios. In one hand, new OFMSW plants 
where URBIOFIN biorefinery approach can be fully implemented, and existing OFMSW plants (producing compost and/or biogas) 
where all or one or more modules of the URBIOFIN biorefinery approach can be added to the available facility. To have a 
successful business is key to integrate bio-based product end-users in order to offer customers not only equipment for building-
blocks or final bio-based products production but also commodity/end product buyers. Despite the URBIOFIN consortium includes 
intermediate and end-users companies other end-users of similar profile are considered customers as well.  
Customer relationships. Access to building or exploitation contracts is only possible through public tenders for building new 
OFMSW treatment plants, or renewing existing facilities. Therefore, the consortium will invest resources (networking, visitin g, 
tradeshows, etc.) to interact with public authorities and improve position and knowledge of upcoming tenders. URBIOFIN offer is 
of special interest for Public Procurement of Innovation (PPI). PPI occurs when public authorities act as a launch customer for 
innovative goods or services. These are typically not yet available on a large -scale commercial basis and may include 
conformance testing as in the case of URBIOFIN.   
Channels. Priority to apply in public tenders for building OFMSW plants  is given to URBIOFIN participant companies, specially 
to URBASER that implement OFMSW plants worldwide. But if this company refuses to apply, agreements with other waste 
companies (i.e. in countries where URBASER is not operating) could be reached  to increase number and quality of channels . 
Networking with other EU waste companies is being considered in the business implementation  via technology licensing or 
specific agreements. A similar approach has been proposed for bio-based final products. Priority is given for example to NATRUE 
to buy the produced cosmetic packages. NATRUE (project partner) represents companies from an emerging market in the EU. 
NATRUE has been – and continues to be – involved in different projects in the fields of scientific research/innovation and 
regulatory affairs where it provides expertise. In this manner, NATRUE actively plays a key role in addressing both challenge s

and opportunities in the Natural and Organic Cosmetics sector. The association nowadays has 49 members quotes Companies

The same for building blocks like PHA where priority is given to LEYGATECH. But if URBIOFIN companies refuse to buy the bio-
based intermediates or final biobased products produced by the customers, then, other EU end -users of a similar profile would 
be integrated via licence or other commercial agreement in order to always provide customers a reliable market uptake of thei r

or agri-cooperatives and farmers.   
Key activities : Feasibility studies, a pplying to publi c tenders, d esigning, engineering, building up  and commissioning, post -
service, creating demand for biobased products, partnering and networking. 
Key resources Most important resources for the business development are project results and capacities and experience of the

Project results at demonstration scale are key resources for the business development: There are bioethanol and bioethylene

process control and engineering of the integrated URBIOFIN process

and future commercialisation, having into account the specific rules and IP protection of each partner that will be included in the

✓ MUNICIPAL WASTE EUROPE  is the European association representing municipalities responsible for waste 
management and their publicly owned waste management companies, promoting public responsibility for waste 
management as a service of general interest. The members are national public waste associations and similar national 
or regional associations. They are committed to a sustainable waste management that minimise the impact on the 
environment and promote resource efficiency, taking into account local conditions. Municipal Waste Europe promotes 
the interests of its members at European level, through a joint position towar ds the EU institutions, and keeps its 
members informed on the latest EU policy developments. The association encourages the sharing of information among 
the members and the exchange of good practices in the local management of waste. 
✓ COPA-COGECA representi ng EU agri -Cooperatives to help market uptake of bio ethylene as a  fruit ripening gas, 
agricultural plastics and liquid and solid fertilisers. In 2013, there were 10.8 million agricultural holdings within the  EU-
28. An analysis by economic size shows that among these there were 6.5 million (or 59.8%) that had a standard output in 
excess of EUR  2 000. In terms of utilised agricultural area, France and Spain had the largest share of the EU -28’s 
agricultural land, with 15.9 % and 13.3 % shares respectively, while the United Kingdom and Germany had shares just 
under 10.0 %. By contrast, the largest number of agricultural holdings was in Romania (3.6 million), where one third 
                                                                             BBI 2016-D6

(13.2 %), some way ahead of Italy (9.3 %) and Spain (8.9 %). 
✓ EUROPEAN BIOPLASTIC eV. represents  the interests of the thriving bioplastics industry. European Bioplastics 
is committed to driving the evolution of plastics by raisin g awareness across all relevant stakeholder groups about the 
benefits of bioplastics in reducing our dependency on fossil resources, reducing harmful greenhouse gas emissions, and 
using renewable resources more efficiently. European Bioplastics is uniquely  placed in the industry with an extensive 
network of businesses, partners, and experts in the bioplastics sector across Europe and beyond.

Economic data. 
The following table shows the economical data of the expected benefits by URBIOFIN partners due to the commercialisation of 
the technology (20 years projected). An estimate has been done with a medium plant capacity of 50,000 ton OFMSW per year, 
which corresponds to an average city of 1,000,000 habitants. 
Table 3.1d URBIOFIN expected benefits 
 
It is expected that once the first biorefinery is installed the technology sales increase. In any case, it is worth to consid er we are 
addressing an extremely large industry (hundred billion €) so the data shown in the table can be considered moderate.  Personnel 
plan has been estimated using revenues per employee as a metric. 62 (Every 305,170 € increase in turnover will require the 
recruitment of one new employee). With the aim of future commercialisation of the technology a viability analysis based on two 
business cases has been done: 
Business case 1 It is studied the complete implantation of a biorefinery for a 50,000 ton OFMSW/year treated, where the incomes 
from bioethylene, PHA, liquid and solid biofertiliser and biome thane have been included.  The expenses are associated to the 
operational costs and amortization costs from plant investment (Plant cost of 13 ,650,000 €, 10 years amortization time, 5% of 
interest). In this case the payback for the urban biorefinery is 3 years, and the return on investment (ROI) is around 30%. 
Table 3.1e URBIOFIN data business 1 
 
Business Case 2 It is studied the partial implantation of the urban biorefinery into an existing MSW treatment plant, which already 
has a biogas and solid fertiliser units. In this the modules are: bioethanol, bioethylene, VFAs, MCFAs, PHA, microalgae and 
aminoacids production units.  In this case the estimated plant investment is 10 ,950,000€. The expenses are associated to the 
operational costs and amortization costs (10 years amortization time, 5% of interest). In this case the payback for the urban  
biorefinery is 2.5 years, and the ROI is around 55%. 
In any of the previous cases the reimbursement from the waste disposal fees has been taken into account for the business 
profitability. In case of including the profitability of the business will increase, depending the tax rate (50-90 € t-1 MSW). On 
average, the payback for the URBIOFIN Biorefinery is 2-4 years. An increase in turnover often requires additional staff. Based 
in the URBIOFIN plant business model and business cases, around 135 employees will be created, in particular, 8 in technological 
development and 15 employees per plant with 8 projected plants in the next five years. 960 will be expected in 2035. In order to 
ensure a successful market penetration, the consortium has identified the first end-user for the roll-out stage. The Eco-Innovative 
technological solution will be fully implemented at commercial scale in Urbaser installations and in Municipalities of 
ACRPLUS organization.

Implementation strategy. 
The implementation strategy of the biorefinery technology is based on the different points agreed in the Consortium Agreement. 
Each partner protected the IP of the demonstrated technology developed in the different Biorefinery units. The implementation  
strategy needs to have into account the different points and actors for the technology commercialization plan development: 
1. Create a specific multidisciplinary team in charge of the commercialization Biorefinery technology. This team has  to be 
composed by people from the consortium companies with experience in the waste management, biotechnological process and 
bioproducts commercialization among others.  The commercialization team will actively participate in the communication, 
dissemination and exploitation act ivities of the URBIOFIN project in order to reach potential clients that have interest in 
implementing the technology at industrial scale in the medium term (1 to 3 years after end of the project).  
2. The main objective for the technology implementation is to build up the first industrial operation plant to integrate the technology 
in the MSW treatment market. With this purpose financing opportunities will be inquired (EU financial opportunities for firt industrial 
plants, etc)  
3. Develop a Specialist Company u nit for the direct production and commercialisation of the technology, using the IP of the 
consortium companies in order to offer a complete and integrate Biorefinery solution for the OFMSW treatment.

3.2 Management structure and procedures 
3.2.1 Organisational structure and decision making 
Figure 3.2a shows the URBIOFIN management structure, which is explained in detail below. 
 
 
Figure 3.2a Overview of URBIOFIN management structure 
The Steering Committee (SC) will have the overall responsibility of the project and will consist of one senior representative from 
each partner. The SC will be in charge of complying with the Grant Agreement and monitoring project progress against description 
of work. A SC meeting will take place every 6 months and the Project Technical Assistant appointed by the EC will be invited to 
attend. During these meetings, the progress achieved in the project objectives and in every Work Package will be presented, 
whereas the work plan will be defined for the next semester. The Project Coordinator (IMECAL) will have a main role in the 
coordination of the board and in cooperation with the other members of the Steering Committee will be in charge of: A) Content, 
finances and intellectual property rights definition (in close collaboration with the IPR Manager (BCM)) A.1) Collection of financial 
information fro m the partners and the provision of regular periodic reports to the BBI JU . A.2) Changes/setting up to the 
Consortium Agreement. A.3) . Looking for the proper potential investors in closed collaboration with the Exploitation Manager 
(BCM), interested in the project results. B) Organization of all Consortium meetings, Review Meetings and events. C) Evolution 
of the Consortium. D) Discussion and solving of business and technical problems that may arise in conjunction with the Scientific 
and Technical Committee, Innovation Committee and Business Committee. The SC will take decisions towards mitigation of risks 
that might jeopardize the effective progress of the project. E) Monitoring of results and establishment contacts with other relevant 
projects, clusters or initiatives (include samples related to objectives of the project). F) Developing the project dissemination and 
exploitation strategy under the hat of the Exploitation, Communication and Dissemination Manager. Each Member of the SC has 
one vote. 
The Project Coordinator (PC) will be responsible for the administrative, financial and organizational management of the project 
as a whole and will be the point of contact with the BBI JU. In URBIOFIN, the project coordinator will be IMECAL, represented by 
Ms Caterina Coll. She has extensive knowledge and expertise in the area of EU funding and project management and relevant 
expertise in the field of Waste Management and Renewable Technologies. Additionally, at the start of the project, a Financial  
Manager from the coordinating organisation will be assigned to support the project coordinator in the project coordination. The 
Project Coordinator shall have as responsibilities: A) Overall responsibility for the project; guarantees its continuity and 
consistency and all ocates its resources adequately. B) Handles any conflict resolution within the project, which could not be 
handled at a lower level. C) Monitors compliance by the parties with their obligations. D) Keeps the address list of members and 
other contact persons updated and available. E) Collects, reviews and submits information on the progress of the project and 
reports and other deliverables (including financial statements and related certification) to the BBI JU. F) Acts as the speaker of 
the project in all i nteractions with the EC and third parties. G) Consolidates the project planning, milestones reports, cost 

                                                                             BBI 2016-D6                                                
745785 URBIOFIN - Part B - 47 
 
 
statements and budget. H) Communicates with work packages in order to guarantee smooth progress and avoid delays in 
deliverables and milestones. The P C will act to mitigate the impact caused for these potential delays. If these issues are not 
resolved satisfactorily, these will be raised with the SC. I) Transmits promptly documents, minutes of the Steering Committee , 
Scientific and Technical Committee, Innovation Committee and Business Committee and information connected with the project. 
J) Monitors the implementation of decisions taken at consortium, SC, S&TC, IC and BC meetings. 
The Scientific & Technical Committee (S&TC) will be responsible for the technical progress of the project; it will comprise the 
leaders of each technical work package and will be chaired by AINIA. In close collaboration with the S&T Manager the Validation 
Manager (URBASER) will be responsible for ensuring a successful demonstration and validation of the innovative solutions. The 
S&TC will have significant role and will be responsible for the coordination of the technical aspects of the project and the proper 
identification of all interfaces. At management level, the mai n role of the S&TC will be to identify effective technical risk 
management in close collaboration with the Risk Manager ( IMECAL); means for follow up the technical achievements in the 
project and for technical decision support. The chair of the S&TC will organize technical meetings every 3 months with the 
cooperation of the work-package leaders. The main tasks of the S&TC are: A) Responsible for technical and scientific progress 
of the project and for completing successfully the S&T objectives and activities of the project in a timely manner. B) Responsible 
for the adequate focus and co-ordination of technical work within the consortium. C) Provide links of the project with other efforts, 
projects and overall initiatives that are related to the theme o f the project either from within the enterprises or outside of the 
enterprises at a national or international level. D) When necessary, e.g. due to a technological breakthrough, adjusts the content 
and direction of research. E) Identify possible technical problems and conflicts between the WPs that may restrain the projects 
technical evolution and will convoke a meeting for their resolution F) The S&TC is expected to meet in average 4 times a year . 
Telephone and web meetings will be used complementary to the physical meetings for keeping close track to the development of 
the subprojects. At the S&TC Meetings the WP Leaders will report the work status following the decision taking procedure 
established. The S&T Manager can request an urgent Steering Committee meeting to the Project Coordinator in case a strategic 
decision related to a Scientific or technical matter has to be made. 
The Innovation Committee (IC) will be responsible for increasing of the innovation level in the consortium, in RTD activities, in 
the business models, with a consequent harmonisation of the whole project management; it will comprise representative of each 
partner and will be chaired by IMECAL. The Innovation Manager (IM) will be responsible for advising the SC on contingency 
implementation. IMECAL will manage risk across the partnership and work packages. This will include maintenance of the risk 
table as well as the implementation of approved contingency actions. In close collaboration with the IC Manager, the Exploitation, 
Dissemination & Communication Manag er (ED&CM) represented by BCM, as major orchestrator of the internal processes of 
project management will have three main roles: A) The ED&CM will contribute developing and managing the dissemination 
strategy, monitoring the results and establishing contac ts with other relevant project. Moreover, the ED&CM manager will be in 
charge for the organisation of Workshops, conferences, training sessions and other events relevant to project promotion. B) A s 
responsible of exploitation strategy, the ED&CM will manag e the promotion of the solutions developed during the project. The 
ED&CM will look for potential stakeholders and investors, interested in the project results, and will be constantly in contac t with 
the public administration, to promote follow -up activities. C) In charge for Knowledge management and Intellectual Property 
Rights, the ED&CM will be available for discussions regarding IPR with the partners at any time during the project. To avoid the 
creation of conflicts with regard to rights of use and comme rcialisation of certain IPR arising from the project, the partners will, 
during the negotiation of the grant agreement, conduct due diligence to determine whether any partner has pre-existing obligations 
with respect to specific IPR. Intellectual Property Rights (IPR) is a major management issue in the exploitation and dissemination 
of scientific project results. Once a year, the Innovation Manager and the ED&CM will assemble the SC. Together, they will review 
the results generated by the project and update  the exploitation plan. The management of IPR will involve: a) Identification of 
patentable research findings b) Evaluation of whether to file for IPR protection or not c) Preparation of applications for IP R 
protection d) Determination of the rights of use for each single Innovative solution of the URBIOFIN project e) Exploitation of the 
IPR generated by the partners.  
The Business Committee (BC) will be responsible for developing a business strategy to take the project results closer to market 
including the identification of post project funding needs and funding opportunities. It will comprise representative of each partner 
and will be chaired by IMECAL, who will lead on the development of the commercialisation strategy in consultation with the 
different stakeholders within the consortium in order to facilitate commercial exploitation by the ED&CM. The BC will meet once 
a year to review the SC results generated by the project and update the business plan.  
The Advisory Board constitutes a consultation body that will comprise well-reputed experts in the sector of waste management, 
biomaterials, as well as municipalities’ representatives. Its purpose is to provide advice and guidance to the project. Furthermore, 
the Advisory Bo ard will ensure that the project management is constantly informed of significant changes in the knowledge 
domains and markets underpinning the project activities. The Advisory Board will operate mostly remotely in so called Virtual  
Joint Sessions exploiti ng teleconference facilities and/or via (e -) mail based interaction, but it will meet possibly at least three 
                                                                             BBI 2016-D6                                                
745785 URBIOFIN - Part B - 48 
 
 
times in the project life span (at the beginning: M3, mid-way through: M31 and at the end: M55) by arrangement at venues to be 
agreed by members with the coordinating party in the composition that would most fit the needs of the meeting. 
The WP leaders (WPL) will be in charge of the implementation of the R&D activities at the WP level. The WPLs will be 
responsible for the coordination, planning, and monitoring of their work packages, i.e. they will coordinate the activities between 
the different partners collaborating on that WP and facilitate information exchange. Every WPL will also examine the deliverables 
provided by the partners from his/her WP and ensure that they are produced with the appropriate quality, on time and according 
to the budget. The WPLs will hold teleconferences as required with the PC, the SC and the S&TM. In summary, their main roles 
will be: A) To manage the scientific  and technical advancement of the WPs. B) To report and prepare proposals for the S&TM 
considering S&T aspects and to report and prepare proposals for the SC with regard to the achievements of the work plan and 
major budget allocations. 
3.2.2 Innovation management 
As URBIOFIN is a project with ambitious technological aims, the consortium needs to be ensured that in 4 years’ time the solution 
will still correspond to the market needs and represent an innovative technological approach, successfully replicated  and 
demonstrated. To achieve this, the URBIOFIN consortium shall make effort to understand and face both market and technical 
problems. The management strategy is recognized as a key factors for succeed in this aspect. Therefore, a special attention will 
be given to the following main managerial aspects (efforts are calculated for all of them in the budget):  
- At innovation and market side: A) A large industrial network will be brought to the consortium and project results in order to 
be sure that a leading market solution could be provided not more than 1 year period after the project end. For this purpose the 
consortium set -up 2 consultative bodies that shall ensure the project innovation, test the solution and provide additional 
requirements and know-how related to their own business processes. The consultative bodies are represented by the Innovation 
Committee and the Business Committee. B) Clear business plan and ownership rights agreement set -up still at the project 
beginning. C) A separate Exploitation Manager (BCM) experience in companies’ creation and business development will support 
the team during the entire project life-cycle.  
- At technical side: A) Requirements managements methodology set up from the project beginning: the experience achieved in 
large scaled research and innovation projects shows a clear need to identify method for ensuring the requirements management 
and proper validation when interdisciplinary research. It shall be specific for the project objectives but not consuming a lo t of 
personnel efforts as standard requirements engineering methods. B) Set -up an integration plan with respect to the interfaces 
management: follow up of the interfaces and setting up a plan with maturity levels for achievements for the entire solution 
integration will lead to a better cooperation, reporting among partners and objective oriented decisions-taken.
3.3 Consortium as a whole 
The project consortium includes 16 partners from 8 countries worldwide at almost all relevant levels (industrial, scientific and 
agricultural sectors) with broad and diverse wealth of experience of project partners and associated partners to allow co-creation 
(multi-actor approach). The integration of 8  countries into the project enables a widespread and country -specific view on the 
handling of MSW as well as about market strategies from different approaches. All consortium partners have extensive experience 
in European and international programmes and projects (see Table 1.3b and section 4). They are experienced in working efficiently 
within a consortium and will bring specific and complementary expertise. The consortium includes partners from research 
organisations, and academic sector combined with a high share of  SME and industrial sector. 10 from 15 project partners are 
involved as SME/industrial project partner with a share of total budget of approx 50%, as well as the leader is a SME partner. 
The industrial partners are involved to support the selected innovative approaches, to give technical assessment, to support the 
further technological development, to implement the project results and to support their marketability.  
The consortium is well equipped to work together to develop different work packages and to secure the commitment for the 
implementation of the joint activities. 6 of eight work packages will be organised by female WP leader (see paragraph 1.3.5). 
All parties will contribute to the project in a meaningful way and ensure that the geographical spread will be beneficial for the  
impact and sustainability of the collaboration and coordination of research programmes in Europe  and abroad. Table 3.3a  
describes the involved project partners and their main tasks within the project. 
Table 3.3a Partners role 
Participant  Role 
IMECAL IMECAL is the coordinator of URBIOFIN project. IMECAL will lead WP2 regarding the conversion of OFMSW to 
bioethanol as building block for the production of bioethylene, and will hold the corresponding demonstration activities in 
its PERSEO semi -industrial plant. IMECAL will also participate in WP1, WP6 and WP7 and will lead WP8 as project 
manager. 
                                                                             BBI 2016-D6                                                
745785 URBIOFIN - Part B - 49 
 
 
AINIA 
Ainia will be focused in the development of two phase AD systems and in the VFA valorisation throughout the conversion 
of VFA to MCFA and later into PHA. Moreover it will participate in the valorisation of microalgae to biofer tiliser. Ainia will 
participate in almost all WP, except WP2. AINIA will also lead WP6 where the entire urban process will be integrated and 
optimised through virtual simulations as well as the project’s impacts will be assessed (economic, environmental and 
social) along with the study of all the potential regulatory and legal aspects which might impact on the project outcomes.  
URBASER 
URBASER will offer its R&D Center area to install new prototypes or pilot plants which allow the operation and validation 
of innovative technological solutions for the treatment of outlet streams coming from the fermentation process of municipal 
solid wastes, in order to get as much of high -grade valuable products (biopolymers, biomethane, microalgae) and 
maximize the valorisation of the organic fraction o f MSW (OFMSW). In particular, URBASER will participate in the 
anaerobic digestion of OFMSW for VFA production and biogas production through methanogenic steps (WP3, WP4), 
operating its anaerobic digester according to the project needs. Furthermore, Urbaser  will integrate of VFA, PHA 
production and microalgae processes.   
BPE 
Role of BIOMASA includes the participat ion in the following WPs: 1, 4, 5, 6, 7 and 8, being related to biofertilisers  
development from organic fraction and microalgae extracts, under the form of solid and liquid by -products from down -
stream units of Fermentation, AD and Biomethane upgrading. Experimental formulation, legal and technical evaluation, 
as well as demonstration and dissemination activities. 
UVA 
The EnvTech group will be involved in the upgrading of raw biogas to biomethane in photobioreactors, the selective 
removal of siloxanes from biomethane in two phase partitioning bioreactors, the selective remova l of H 2S from biogas 
and its further bioconversion into high -added value products such as PHAs. EnvTech  will apply its 16 years of R&D 
experience in the design and operation of algal -bacterial photobioreactors to optimize the upgrading potential and 
maximize the production of biobased products. The group has successfully operated both open and enclosed 
photobioreactors under indoor and outdoor conditions for the treatment of domestic and livestock wastewaters. Besides, 
the broad experience of the EnvTech group in the operation of low -cost, high -efficiency bioreactors for waste gas 
treatment will be applied t o the selective removal of siloxanes and H 2S, and to the bioconversion of the raw biogas to 
high-added value products. 
NOVO 
Novozymes will sample enzyme products optimized for degradation of MSW and provide recommendations for 
optimization of enzyme application in the Perseo Bioethanol® process to enable cost -efficient conversion of MSW to 
sugars for further downstream processing into higher-value products. 
WR 
Wageningen Research will establish fermentation processes using Cryptococcus sp. for medium/long-chain fatty acid 
(MCFA/LCFA) based on the existing volatile fatty acid (VFA) stream and will establish a ferme ntation process for mcl-
PHA production using the VFAs and bio-ethanol as substrates and pure cultures of Pseudomonas putida as production 
organism. In addition, WR will be responsible for formulating/developing novel composites based on the biomaterials 
deriving from MSW (pulp, mcl-PHA, scl-PHA). 
CIEMAT 
CIEMAT will be focused on adapting/improving the PERSEO bioethanol production process to the new feedstock by 
optimizing pretreatment, enzymatic hydrolysis and fermentation steps. Apart from sugar recovery and ethanol yield, 
energy efficiency ratio, mass b alance and toxic compounds generation will be used for the estimation of the optimized 
parameters. CIEMAT will also assist IMECAL in the analysis of the fractions generated in the demo trials.  
VISUM/ 
IRIS 
VISUM/IRIS will participate in WP2 where they will test novel advanced sensors for monitoring selected process 
parameters and will integrate them at plant level together with a bespoke control system. They will also collaborate in the 
study of the relevant parameters to select the most suitable sensor technologies. They will also develop data mining tools 
to produce relevant decision support tools for optimally controlling production based on relevant process data. VISUM 
will also participate in WP1, supporting the w ork on preliminary actions for biorefinery design which will feed into WP2. 
VISUM will also take part in WP6, in the environmental, economic and regulatory assessments from the monitoring at 
plant scale point of view and will participate in WP7 by actively engaging in exploitation and dissemination tasks. 
NATURE 
PLAST 
Natureplast’s role will mainly be focused on characterizing the raw polymers (PHA) produced by the consortium, and to 
modify them to improve their processability and properties for the target ed applications. 
IRIAF/ 
GEACAM 
IRIAF / GEACAM will be in charge of the VFA valorisation throughout the conversion of VFA to MCFA and later into PHA 
in a demonstrative scale (bioreactor of 20 m3). Also, it will treat with a passive system based on constructed wetlands the 
wastewater generated once the microorganisms that accumulate PHA are separated. 
BCM BCM is WP leader of WP 7 “Dissemination, communication and exploitation activities”.  
LEYGATECH Validation of biopolymers produced at end-user level. The biopolymers will be tested in real manufacturing chains in order 
to produce bags and films suitable for project target sectors. 
NATRUE 
AISBL 
Coordination with supporting member companies from the association:  
- Development of packaging concepts and specifications for cosmetic applications 
- Studies on product-packaging interactions in specific cosmetic product applications 
                                                                             BBI 2016-D6                                                
745785 URBIOFIN - Part B - 50 
 
 
CSIC CSIC will be focused on designing and building a pilot plant downstream for the transformation of the produced bioethanol 
in bioethylene. CSIC will also assist IMECAL in the operation and analysis of the fractions generated in the pilot plant.
3.4 Resources to be committed 
 
Below it is provided a more detailed description of resources allocation for WP2 Conversion of OFMSW to bioethanol as building 
block for the production of bioethylene, WP4 Biogas bioconversion to biomethane and added value products and WP8 Project 
management 
  
- WP2: Conversion of OFMSW to bioethanol as building block for the production of bioethylene 
 
IMECAL is the leader of WP2 and all the pilot plant adaptation, new module building up and demonstration activities of Module 1 
of URBIOFIN biorefinery will be located in its biotechnological demonstration plant (2000 m 2). These activities will include the 
demonstration plant adaptation to improve the feasibility and yield of bioethanol, to adapt the demonstration plant to new 
pretreatments, to adapt the plant to produce bioethanol as building block, the integration of the bioethanol-to-bioethylene unit and 
the development of a new monitoring system (Tasks 2.1. and 2.2). These activities require the involvement of engineers (1) 
technicians (2) and operators (4) in order to design and implement all the plant new modules (pre -treatment, 20 m 3 hydrolysis 
reactor, 50 m3 fermentation reactors, distillation units, and the installation of a new bioethanol-to-bioethylene operation unit). 
  
The demonstration activities planned in WP2 will be carried out during 40 months of the project in a continuous demonstration  
plant with the different raw materials defined in WP1 (Tasks 2.3, 2.4, 2.5). During the demonstration activities at semi -industrial 
scale, which will run in three-shift operation (24 hours a day), continuous results analysis (energy and mass balances, continuous 
process analysis (sugars, ethanol, inhibitors, etc), bioethanol yields, products characterisations, quality controls, etc.) will be 
performed in order to carry out the appropriate redesign of activities, materials dosage, process control, with the aim to im prove 
process performance. During all the demonstration stage several human resources (3 engineers, 3 technicians and 5 operators) 
are needed to cover all activities for the correct implementation of the project schedule. All IMECAL´s activities in WP2 wil l be 
carried out by own company personnel. 
 
- WP4: Biogas bioconversion to biomethane and added value products. 
 
University of Valladolid will be the main responsible for the design, construction, start -up and operation (including process 
monitoring) of 4 demo-scale technology set-ups in WP4 which includes: 1 ) 273 m2 photobioreactor interconnected to a biogas 
scrubbing unit for biomethane production), 2) a 10 m3 combined unit composed of a biotrickling filter coupled with a fermenter to 
bioconvert the H2S free biogas into biopolymers, including a biomass separation unit, adapted to the biogas production of the AD-
PHASE 2, 3) a gradual scale up to a 1 m 3 high mass transfer bioreactor for siloxane removal to polish biomethane. The 4 
technologies are intrinsically different in nature, purposes and monitoring needs, and will be run in continuous mode for at least 
26 months at the R&D center of URBASER in Zaragoza (Spain). These activities, included in Tasks 4.1, 4.3 and 4.4, will require 
a large effort in term of person months from the 5 senior researchers considered (1 full professor, 2 associate professors and 2 
assistant professors) for the design of the d emo-bioreactors (involving ATEX requirements due to the use of biogas as raw 
material), control strategies, process supervision and site visits. The construction, operation and monitoring of these indus trial 
scale units will require the active participatio n of at least 3 researchers and 1 technician hired under the project basis. The 
monitoring of these 4 processes will involve the development and validation of dedicated and time-consuming methodologies for 
the analysis of siloxanes, dynamics of microbial p opulation structure along the 4 year operation (using molecular biology 
techniques) and physical/chemical and instrumental analyses for the determination of the gas and liquid phase concentrations of 
CH4, CO2, O2, N2, H2S, N2O, volatile organic compounds, NH3, NH4+, NO3-, NO2-, SO42-, S2O3-, S2-, HS-, PO43-, total organic carbon, 
inorganic carbon, TKN, Total Nitrogen, Total and Volatile suspended solids, pH, alkalinity, BOD, COD and polyhydroxyalkanoates. 
The large amount of data generated from the optimiza tion of these 4 demo set -ups will also entail a significant effort in data 
analysis and report preparations.   
 
                                                                             BBI 2016-D6                                                
745785 URBIOFIN - Part B - 51 
 
 
 
- WP8: Project management 
 
IMECAL is URBIOFIN coordinator and responsible to manage and assure the optimal implementation of this large innovation -
action project (4 years duration; 16 consortium partners, 4 advisory board members). This includes continuous reporting activities, 
administrative, financial and risk management, progress monitoring and preparation of projects meetings and reports as well as 
the exploitation and innovation management.  
 
In addition to that, it is important to highlight that URBIOFIN project includes several modules that will be interconnected and the 
coordination of them will require specific proactive human resources which would address the potential conflicts inherent to 
interrelated biorefinery technologies' projects. An intensive coordination effort is needed in this point in order to achive the project 
objectives. 
 
The project management requires exclusive staff dedicated to monitoring, quality control and project risk control. This requi res 
specific human resources to perform this control and obtain a successful project result. In this task 2 people are going to be 
involved during all the project time.

4. MEMBERS OF THE CONSORTIUM
4.1 Participants 
 
PARTNER 1. Coordinator 
Name: Industrias Mecanicas Alcudia S.A. 
(IMECAL) 
Web page: www.imecal.com/perseo  
Type: SME 
Country: Spain  
Brief description of the organization:  
IMECAL is a SME which was founded in 1979 as an engineering company in the metal sector, working on demand and 
manufacturing all type of metal -mechanical equipment for civil works, petro -refineries and petrochemical, transportation, 
refrigeration industry, industrial auxiliary motor and ceramics industry, among others. R & D IMECAL Department has allowed 
the company to progress in the technological field, having made significant partnerships with companies, universities and public 
research organizations. The R&D line o f production technology for second generation bioethanol has developed a 
biotechnological patented technology for obtaining bioethanol from Organic Municipal Waste. In 2007 IMECAL built a second 
generation bioethanol plant with a capacity to process 25 ton /day of organic fraction of MSW (PERSEO Bioethanol®). Since 
this year IMECAL has participated in different projects to test and improve PERSEO technology to different MSW raw materials 
with different companies. IMECAL is member of the Biofuels TP Platform-European Union, and participates actively in several 
national and international conferences on biofuels. 
 
Role in the Project:  
IMECAL is the coordinator of URBIOFIN project. IMECAL will lead WP2 regarding the conversion of OFMSW to bioethanol as 
building block for the production of bioethylene, and will hold the corresponding demonstration activities in its PERSEO semi-
industrial plant. IMECAL will also participate in WP1, WP3, WP5, WP6 and WP7, and will lead WP8 as project manager.  
Scientific team:  
Ms. Caterina Coll Lozano, PMP ® (F), Chemical engineer by the Higher Technical School of Industrial Engineers of the 
Polytechnic University of Valencia. Project Management Profesional (PMP®) certificate by Project Management Institute (PMI). 
Executive MBA by Bussines & Marketing School ESIC. Master degree in environment coursed in the Department of Chemical 
and Nuclear Engineering from the Polytechnic University of Valencia. Technical Industrial engineer in Chemist by the Technical 
School of Industrial Engin eering of the Polytechnic University of Valencia. Stay in the "School of Science" of “Institute of 
Technology Sligo" in Sligo (Ireland). Stay on the Biomass Unit of the Division of Renewable Energy from the department of 
Energy of CIEMAT. Professional expe rience of over 15 years in process engineering and environment, mainly developed in 
CEAM (“Centro de Estudios Ambientales del Mediterraneo”) as Head of laboratory and environmental projects, and in IMECAL 
as Plant Manager of second generation bioethanol pi lot plant PERSEO, and R&D Manager. Over the last years he has 
coordinated and participated in several projects at national and international level and performed scientific and technical 
publications in various journals, books and conference contributions. 
Dr. Ing. Marcos Latorre Sánchez  (M) , Chemical Engineer by the Higher Technical School of Industrial Engineers of the 
Polytechnic University of Valencia. Masters in Design for Sustainability from Cranfield University (England). PhD in Green 
Chemistry at Institute of Chemical Technology (Polytechnic University of Valencia - Spanish National Research Council). Stay 
at Max Planck Institute of Colloids and Interfaces (Germany). He has more than 6 years of experience in new materials 
development at laboratory and pilot scale and advanced characterization for renewable energy systems. He has participated 
in a number of R&D nationally and internationally funded projects aimed at the valorisation of biomass into higher valuable 
products. He is author of 10 papers in peer-reviewed journals and has participated in different international conferences. 
Mrs. Sara Castelló Andrés (F), Mrs. Castelló holds a degree in Food Science and Technology (University of Valencia, 2006) 
and a Master in New Functional Foods (Universidad Autónoma de Madrid, 2013). She has 13 years of experience managing

PARTNER 2 
Name: ainia 
Web page: www.ainia.es 
Type: RTO 
Country: SPAIN 
 
Brief description of the organization:  
ainia is a RTD centre focused in the agro-food sector and related industries. Nowadays, ainia has more than 700 food SME´s 
company members of its organization. The aim of the centre is to promote research and technological development in the agro-
food sector, to increase quali ty in production, improve competitiveness and promote modernization and diversification in the 
agro-food industries. This is achieved providing a wide range of technological services to its members, through the execution 
of scientific research projects and technology transfer to the industry. ainia staff is composed by around 180 people.  
The work team involved in this project is formed by Environmental Management researchers with wide experience in areas of 
activity related with the project: development of new biomass pre-treatments, alternative substrates and energy crops, 2-stages 
fermentation, Anaerobic Digestion -biorefineries, VFA and nutrient recovery, reduction of biological risks, digestate -based 
fertilisers, control and modelling of the AD process and advanced microbial characterization. 
 
Role in the Project: ainia will be focused in the development of two phase AD systems and in the VFA valorisation throughout 
the conversion of VFA to MCFA and later into PHA. Moreover it will participate in the valorisation of microalgae to biofertiliser. 
Ainia will participate in all WP, except WP2, and will lead WP1 . AINIA leads the WP6 where the entire urban process will be 
integrated and optimised through virtual simulations as well as the project’s impacts will be assessed (economic, environmental 
and social) along with the study of all the potential regulatory and legal aspects which might impact on the project outcomes. 
Scientific team:  
Sara TENA (F) . Sara is a Chemical Engineer with more than sixteen years´ experience in industry and consultancy. Her 
specialist technical areas include process and energy modelling, techn ical and economic feasibility studies (TEA), project 
concept design, and technical project management. Over the last twelve years Sara has worked as energy engineer and 
consultant for an international engineering firm, delivering multiple TEA studies on en ergy and bioenergy projects, including: 
biogas and biomethane to grid plants; solid biomass combustion; energy from waste; combined heat and power and district 
heating projects. Sara recently joined AINIA as a Project Manager working on biorefinery, bioene rgy and wastewater projects 
and she is currently coordinating the URBIOFIN project internally at AINIA. 
Gracia SILVESTRE (F) is PhD Chemical Engineer and has more than seven years of experience in anaerobic digestion 
technologies with special focus in the co-digestion strategies of organic wastes. Experience in participation and technical 
execution of diverse R&D projects and te chnical assistances in the biogas field. Experience in related projects: SOSTRICE 
project (ongoing; she is involved in researching activities related to demonstration plant testing), AD -WISE project (she was 
involved in calibration activities of the SVFA s ensors for optimized control of AD plants) and SLUDGE4ENERGY project (she 
developed the pilot plant trials using a 2-phase anaerobic digestion pilot plant).  
Paz GÓMEZ (F) is Agricultural Engineer, specialization on Rural Engineering, and has more than eight years of experience on

PARTNER 3 
Name: URBASER S.A.

Type: Large Industry 
Country: SPAIN 
 
Brief description of the organization:  
URBASER belongs to the group ACS (“ Actividades de Construcción y Servicios ”), which is a worldwide reference in 
infrastructures, industrial services, energy and environment. 
The environmental company URBASER is leader in waste management and treatment in Spain. It  specializes in street 
cleaning, waste removal and transporting, urban waste treatment and recycling, waste to energy facilities and comprehensive 
management of the water cycle and urban landscape and gardening.  
URBASER is the leader in removal and treatment of used mineral oils and treatment and removal of industrial waste.  
URBASER covers the entire value chain when providing these services, from designing and conception, carrying out the 
project, construction, financing and operating a highly-qualified professional team.   
URBASER also operates in the field of renewable energies with a view to limiting the negative impact of greenhouse gases, 
for the purpose of which it is developing treatment processes for alternative sources of energy, biomass from bio mass crops, 
waste woodland mass, biodegradable, agricultural and industrial waste. 
Urbaser achieved a business turnover of 1.498 million € in 2010 with a highly -qualified staff of more than 30.000 people and 
over 160 subsidiary companies forming the group.  It provides services to more than 50 million people and is active in 4 
continents. The main magnitudes are as follows:  
•   232 MW installed in renewable sources of energy, with a production of 479 GWh in 2010. 
•   Reducing CO2 production by more than 2.4 t/year. 
•   Treating and removing 4.6 million t/year of inert waste.  
•   Collecting and treating 150,000 t/year of industrial waste.  
•   Treating and regenerating 67,000 t/year of mineral oils. 
•   Annual removal of more than 5 million tons of solid urban waste. 
•   Annual cleaning of more than 8 million kilometers of streets. 
•   Annual maintenance of more than 60 million m² of green zones.

Technical equipment: 
URBASER manages many waste treatment plants, equipped with varied technologies; consequently, it has an experienced 
global vision of the different integrated technologies. At present, URBASER counts on a new Waste Technological Innovation 
R&D Center, called CIAM, focused on testing and studying innovative environmental technologies. This facility, located within 
a big industrial waste treatment plant, consists of different demonstration plants in the field of waste treatment (pre -treatment 
of municipal solid waste, anaerobic digestion of organic matter, composting, solid recovery fuel production and conversion of 
plastic waste into fuel). In addition to the pilot plants, a 250 m 2 testing bench surface at the R&D Center is also available to 
install new prototypes or pilot plants; this testing bench surface is equipped with the necessary utilities like compressed air, 
power supply, water, etc., a leachate collection system and a modern laboratory to analyse samples in order to obtain vital 
information for R&D projects.

PARTNER 5 
Name: University of Valladolid 
Web page: www.uva.es; http://envtech.uva.es;  
http://gastreatment-
microalgaeresearchgroup.blogspot.com.es 
Type: RTO 
Country: SPAIN 
 
Brief description of the organization 
The Environmental Technology Group (EnvTech) from the Department of Chemical Engineering and Environmental 
Technology at the University of Valladolid (UVa) started its research activities in the early 80s in the treatment of industr ial 
wastewaters and biological nutrient removal. Other research lines such as biological gas treatmen t, microalgae -based 
wastewater treatment and biomass valorization were initiated in 2000. Since 1980, the EnvTech has conducted a sustained 
and intense labour in the development of cost -effective technologies for pollution control in both wastewater and of f-gas 
emissions. More than 35 years of expertise in design and operation of wastewater treatment processes, 16 of them related 
to microalgae-based wastewater treatment, biological gas treatment and microalgae valorization, support the capacity of the 
group to conduct the tasks assigned in the URBioFIN project, i.e. biogas upgrading to biomethane in high rate algae ponds 
and subsequent biomass revalorization, biogas desulfurization by biotrickling filtration, removal of siloxanes from raw biogas 
and biogas c onversion into high -added value products. Its research activity has been recognized and financed within the 
frame of public R&D projects from the Spanish Ministry for Science and Education and the EU (42 projects with a total Budget 
of ≈5761000 € in the past 10 years). The research group has also collaborated with several companies aiming at reinforcing 
the mechanisms of knowledge transfer between University and Industry (62 projects with a total Budget of ≈7535000 € in the 
past 10 years). Nowadays, EnvTech is composed of 2 full professors, 8 associate professors, 7 post-docs, 15 PhD students 
and 5 technicians. In addition, the academic and scientific productivity of the group during these past 5 years accounted for 
15 PhD theses presented, 148 JCR articles, 4 patents and 150 contributions to International Congresses. 
 
Role in the Project:  
The EnvTech group will be involved in the upgrading of raw biogas to biomethane in photobioreactors, the selective removal 
of siloxanes from biomethane in two phase partitioning bioreactors, the selective removal of H2S from biogas and its further 
bioconversion into high-added value products such as PHAs. EnvTech will apply its 16 years of R&D experience in the design 
and operation of algal-bacterial photobioreactors to optimize the upgrading potential and maximize the subsequent production 
of biobased products. The group has successfully operated both open and enclosed photobioreactors under indoor and 
outdoor conditions for the treatment of domestic and livestock wastewate rs. Besides, the broad experience of the EnvTech 
group in the operation of low-cost, high-efficiency bioreactors for waste gas treatment will be applied to the selective removal 
of siloxanes and H 2S, and to the bioconversion of the raw biogas to high -added value products. Role of EnvTech includes 
the participation in the following WPs: 1, 4 (leader), 6, 7 and 8. 
Scientific team:  
Dr. Raúl Muñoz  (M), H=31 Dr. Muñoz holds a PhD in Environmental Biotechnology from Lund University (2005). Raúl is 
Associate Professor at the Department of Chemical Engineering and Environmental Technology at UVa. His main fields of 
expertise are wastewater treatment in algal-bacterial photobioreactors and biological gas treatment. Over the past 10 years, 
Raúl has published 124 ISI papers, 22 book chapters, 105 International Conference proceedings and supervised 11 PhD 
theses and 16 Master theses. Raúl has been Principal Investigator in 21 R&D projects and contracts with companies in the 
past 10 years. 
Dr. Silvia Bolado Rodriguez  (F), H=14 PhD in Chemistry at UVa in 1995, and Associate Professor at the Department of 
Chemical Engineering and Environmental Technology at UVa. She has an extensive experience in solid waste pretreatment, 
valorization and separation processes. She has participated in more than 50 R&D public and private projects, coordinating 
20 of them. Nowadays, she is Principal Investigator in 2 research projects on valoriz ation of microalgae biomass grown in 
wastewater. She has more than 70 scientific publications, 37 ISI papers, 9 book chapters, 2 books and 60 International 
Conferences. She has supervised 9 PhD theses.   
Dr. Pedro A. García Encina  (M), H= 27, PhD in Chemistry at UVa in 1985, he has an extensive experience in the 
development of biological nutrient removal processes and the application of molecular tools. In the past years Pedro A. 
García Encina has been principal investigator in 3 National R&D projects in microalgae-based wastewater treatment. Pedro 
is Full Professor at UVa and has published more than 75 ISI papers and supervised 19 PhD students in his research career. 
Pedro has been Principal Investigator in more than 50 R&D public and private projects.

Dr. Raquel Lebrero (F), H=11, holds a PhD in Chemical Engineering from UVa in 2013 and her field of expertise is biological 
gas treatment with a particular focus on gas-liquid mass transfer phenomena. She is Assistant Professor at the Department

Brief description of the organization:  
Exergy is one of the UK's leading renewable energy companies with the expertise to provide services, across the globe, to 
develop, engineer, construct and operate projects that contribute to our goal of a low carbon, sustainable future. We have been 
in the industry for over 10 years, contributing to the development of the global renewable energy market. We have helped to 
move the sustainable energy debate from the margin to the mainstream. Operating across a range of innovative low -carbon 
energy technologies, our capabilities cover everything from project inception to energy generation and operation. Sustainability 
lies at the core of our values; balancing commercial, environmental and social concerns to address the world’s energy problems 
is what makes us different. 
We are unique in our ability to offer vertically integrated skills in a range of sustainable energy technologies. Exergy can be 
involved at every stage: from project design and development, through planning and financing, engineering and construction 
to operation. Exergy ensures schemes are designed and built to generate energy in the most economical way and with minimal 
environmental impact. 
Exergy provides a range of technical and professional services across the chemical, energy and built environment sector by 
means of a multi -disciplinary team supported by extensive practical experience in the following specialist areas: Feasibilit y 
Assessments that include techno -economic assessments and LCC; Design, Modelling and Scaling up of Chemical and 
Biochemical Processes; Resource Efficiency & Environmental Management; Water Management Strategies; Design and 
Delivery of Resource Efficiency support for SME’s; Development, Monitoring and Measurement of Sustainability Projects; Low 
Carbon footprint Construction Techniques and Life Cycle Assessment. Exergy has a strong work team made up of different 
profiles: chemical and process engineers, mechanical engineers, civil engineers and environmental engineers, amongst other. 
Exergy is also member of SPIRE and BIC. 
 
Role in the Project : Exergy leads the WP6 where the entire urban process will be integrated and optimised through virtual 
simulations as well as the project’s impacts will be assessed (economic, environmental and social) along with the study of al l 
the potential regulatory and legal aspects which might impact on the project outcomes.  Role of Exergy includes also the 
participation in the following WPs: 1, 7 and 8.

Brief description of the organization:  
Novozymes is a world leader in bio-innovation and specialised in industrial enzymes and microorganisms. NZ already markets 
over 700 biotechnology products in 130 countries.  The enzyme production leaves NZ with a global enzyme market share of 
48% (2015). Around 14% of NZ revenue is spent on research and development, and it currently holds almost 7,000 granted or 
pending patents, which indicate the possibilities when nature and technology join forces. As a leading biotech company, NZ 
believes that by using industrial biotechnology thousands of everyday products can potentially be re -engineered to deliver 
enhanced sustainability performance, at no extra cost. Over the past 15 years, the company has invested heavily in developing 
superior enzyme products to enable the biomass and MSW to bioethanol/biogas industry as well as the generation of simple 
sugars from lignocellulose for the bio -production of more advanced products. Novozymes is today supplying enzymes to the 
majority of existing lignocellulosic bio-ethanol plants. 
 
Role in the Project:  
Novozymes will sample enzyme products optimized for degradation of MSW and provide recommendations for optimization of 
enzyme application in the Perseo Bioethanol® process to enable cost -efficient conversion of MSW to sugars for further 
downstream processing into higher-value products. Role of Novozymes includes the participation in the following WPs:  1, 2, 
6, 7 and 8.

PARTNER 9 
Name: Wageningen University & Research 
Web page: http://www.wur.nl/es.htm 
Type: RTO 
Country: The
